 reorganizations and mergers with businesses or entities that desire to avoid what such entities may deem to be the adverse factors related to an initial public offering (&#147;IPO&#148;) as a method of going public. The most prevalent of these factors include substantial time requirements
 legal and accounting costs
 the inability to obtain an underwriter who is willing to publicly offer and sell shares
 the lack of or the inability to obtain the required financial statements for such an undertaking
 state limitations on the amount of dilution to public investors in comparison to the shareholders of any such entities
 along with other conditions or requirements imposed by various federal and state securities laws
 rules and regulations and federal and state agencies that implement such laws
 rules and regulations.


 along with required audited
 interim and proforma financial statements
 within four business days of the closing of any such transaction (Item 5.01(a)(8) of Form 8-K); and the recent amendments to Rule 144 adopted by the SEC that were effective on February 15
 2008
 limit the resale of most securities of shell companies until one year after the filing of such information
 may eliminate many of the perceived advantages of these types of going public transactions.&nbsp;&nbsp;These types of transactions are customarily referred to as &#147;reverse&#148; mergers in which the acquired company&#146;s shareholders become controlling shareholders in the acquiring company and the acquiring company becomes the successor to the business operations of the acquired company.&nbsp;&nbsp;Regulations governing shell companies also deny the use of Form S-8 for the registration of securities and limit the use of this Form to a reorganized shell company until the expiration of 60 days from when any such entity is no longer considered to be a shell company.&nbsp;&nbsp;This prohibition could further restrict opportunities for us to acquire companies that may already have stock option plans in place that cover numerous employees.&nbsp;&nbsp;In such instances
 there may be no exemption from registration for the issuance of securities in any business combination to these employees
 thereby necessitating the filing of a registration statement with the SEC to complete any such reorganization
 and incurring the time and expense that are normally avoided by reverse mergers.


 adopted by the SEC and effective on February 15
 2008
 codify the SEC&#146;s prior position limiting the tradeability of certain securities of shell companies
 including those issued by us in any acquisition
 reorganization or merger
 and further limit the tradeability of additional securities of shell companies; these amendments further restrict the availability of opportunities for us to acquire any business or enterprise that desires to utilize us as a means of going public.

 2008. The Company was originally formed to engage in the business of marketing

 and had no significant assets.&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company abandoned the proprietary bottled water business in 2010. &nbsp;In May

 Inc. (n/k/a Kuboo
 Inc.) acquired 80% of the Company&#146;s issued and outstanding common stock
 and

&#148; which requires accounting for deferred income taxes under the asset and liability method. &nbsp;Deferred income tax assets and liabilities are computed for the difference between the financial statement and tax bases of assets and liabilities that will result in taxable or deductible amounts in the future based on the enacted tax laws and rates applicable to the periods in which the differences are expected to affect taxable income. &nbsp;Valuation allowances are established
 when necessary
 to reduce the deferred income tax assets to the amount expected to be realized.


 the use of estimates
 and the interpretation and application of complex tax laws. &nbsp;Significant judgment is required in assessing the timing and amounts of deductible and taxable items and the probability of sustaining uncertain tax positions. &nbsp;The benefits of uncertain tax positions are recorded in the Company&#146;s financial statements only after determining a more-likely-than-not probability that the uncertain tax positions will withstand challenge
 if any
 from tax authorities. &nbsp;When facts and circumstances change
 the Company reassesses these probabilities and records any changes in the consolidated financial statements as appropriate.







 the Company is required to determine whether a tax position of the Company is more likely than not to be sustained upon examination by the applicable taxing authority
 including resolution of any related appeals or litigation processes
 based on the technical merits of the position. &nbsp;The tax benefit to be recognized is measured as the largest amount of benefit that is greater than fifty percent likely of being realized upon ultimate settlement. &nbsp;De-recognition of a tax benefit previously recognized could result in the Company recording a tax liability that would reduce stockholders&#146; equity.

 2011

 under the SPA
 if the Buyer did not complete certain transactions within the time period prescribed by the SPA
 the Buyer would be obligated to pay the Company an additional $50
000 in cash. The transactions were not completed within the prescribed time period. &nbsp;The Company has not yet received any additional payment from the Buyer.


 2011
 the Company also entered into a Principal Shareholders Agreement with each of the Principal Shareholders dated as of May 27
 2011 (&#147;PSA&#148;)
 under which the Company agreed to make payments to the Principal shareholders in the aggregate amount of $250
000
 in consideration of the Principal Shareholders&#146; undertakings in the SPA
 including but not limited to their agreement to indemnify the Buyer in connection with the stock purchase contemplated in the SPA. &nbsp;If the Buyer makes the additional $50
000 payment referenced above
 then the Company is required to pay such additional $50
000 to the Principal Shareholders in accordance with the PSA. The Company has not received any additional payment from the Buyer. Although the Company believes that it is not required to make the additional $50
000 payment to the Principal Shareholders until it receives such payment from the Buyer
 the Company has recorded a corresponding liability in the amount of $50
000. &nbsp;Each of the Principal Shareholders was a significant shareholder of the Company
 and
 in addition

 our President and Secretary/Treasurer concluded that our disclosure controls and procedures as of the end of the period covered by the Annual Report were effective such that the information required to be disclosed by us in reports filed under the Exchange Act is (i)&nbsp;recorded

 including our President and Secretary/Treasurer
 as appropriate to allow timely decisions regarding disclosure. A controls system cannot provide absolute assurance
 however
 that the objectives of the controls system are met
 and no evaluation of controls can provide absolute assurance that all control issues and instances of fraud
 if any
 within a company have been detected.






 internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements. Therefore
 even those systems determined to be effective can provide only reasonable assurance of achieving their control objectives.


 2013.&nbsp;&nbsp;In making this assessment
 our management used the criteria set forth by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission (&#147;COSO&#148;) in Internal Control&nbsp;- Integrated Framework (1992).&nbsp;&nbsp;Based on this evaluation
 our President and Secretary/Treasurer
 concluded that
 as of December&nbsp;31

 based on having insufficient resources to establish an effective control environment during 2013.

 as well as their related disclosures. &amp;nbsp;Such estimates and assumptions also affect the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting period. &amp;nbsp;Actual results could differ from those estimates.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&lt;i&gt;Cash and Cash Equivalents&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;The Company considers short-term interest bearing investments with initial maturities of three months or less to be cash equivalents. Cash and cash equivalents consist of cash in banks
 free credit on investment accounts and money market accounts. &amp;nbsp;The Company has no cash or cash equivalents.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&lt;i&gt;Income Taxes&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;The Company&amp;#146;s taxable income or loss is included in the consolidated income tax returns of the Company&amp;#146;s parent. Current and deferred income taxes are allocated to the members of the consolidated group as if each member were a separate taxpayer. The Company accounts for income taxes in accordance with FASB ASC Topic 740 &amp;#147;Income Taxes
&amp;#148; which requires accounting for deferred income taxes under the asset and liability method. &amp;nbsp;Deferred income tax assets and liabilities are computed for the difference between the financial statement and tax bases of assets and liabilities that will result in taxable or deductible amounts in the future based on the enacted tax laws and rates applicable to the periods in which the differences are expected to affect taxable income. &amp;nbsp;Valuation allowances are established
 when necessary
 to reduce the deferred income tax assets to the amount expected to be realized.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;The determination of the Company&amp;#146;s provision for income taxes requires significant judgment
 the use of estimates
 and the interpretation and application of complex tax laws. &amp;nbsp;Significant judgment is required in assessing the timing and amounts of deductible and taxable items and the probability of sustaining uncertain tax positions. &amp;nbsp;The benefits of uncertain tax positions are recorded in the Company&amp;#146;s financial statements only after determining a more-likely-than-not probability that the uncertain tax positions will withstand challenge
 if any
 from tax authorities. &amp;nbsp;When facts and circumstances change
 the Company reassesses these probabilities and records any changes in the consolidated financial statements as appropriate.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;In accordance with GAAP
 the Company is required to determine whether a tax position of the Company is more likely than not to be sustained upon examination by the applicable taxing authority
 including resolution of any related appeals or litigation processes
 based on the technical merits of the position. &amp;nbsp;The tax benefit to be recognized is measured as the largest amount of benefit that is greater than fifty percent likely of being realized upon ultimate settlement. &amp;nbsp;De-recognition of a tax benefit previously recognized could result in the Company recording a tax liability that would reduce stockholders&amp;#146; equity.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;This policy also provides guidance on thresholds
 measurement
 de-recognition
 classification
 interest and penalties
 accounting in interim periods
 disclosure
 and transition that is intended to provide better financial statement comparability among different entities. &amp;nbsp;Management&amp;#146;s conclusions regarding this policy may be subject to review and adjustment at a later date based on factors including
 but not limited to
 on-going analyses of and changes to tax laws
 regulations and interpretations thereof. &amp;nbsp;Generally
 the tax filings are no longer subject to income tax examinations by major taxing authorities for years before 2009. Any potential examinations may include questioning the timing and amount of deductions
 the nexus of income among various tax jurisdictions and compliance with U.S. federal
 state and local tax laws.&amp;nbsp; The Company&apos;s management does not expect that the total amount of unrecognized tax benefits will materially change over the next twelve months. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&lt;i&gt;Interest and Penalty Recognition on Unrecognized Tax Benefits&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;The Company recognizes interest accrued related to unrecognized tax benefits in interest expense and penalties in other operational expenses. No interest expense or penalties have been recognized as of and for the years ended December 31
 2013 and 2012.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&lt;i&gt;Fair Value of Financial Instruments&lt;/i&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;The fair values of the Company&amp;#146;s assets and liabilities that qualify as financial instruments under FASB ASC Topic 825

&amp;#148; which requires accounting for deferred income taxes under the asset and liability method. &amp;nbsp;Deferred income tax assets and liabilities are computed for the difference between the financial statement and tax bases of assets and liabilities that will result in taxable or deductible amounts in the future based on the enacted tax laws and rates applicable to the periods in which the differences are expected to affect taxable income. &amp;nbsp;Valuation allowances are established
 when necessary
 to reduce the deferred income tax assets to the amount expected to be realized.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;The determination of the Company&amp;#146;s provision for income taxes requires significant judgment
 the use of estimates
 and the interpretation and application of complex tax laws. &amp;nbsp;Significant judgment is required in assessing the timing and amounts of deductible and taxable items and the probability of sustaining uncertain tax positions. &amp;nbsp;The benefits of uncertain tax positions are recorded in the Company&amp;#146;s financial statements only after determining a more-likely-than-not probability that the uncertain tax positions will withstand challenge
 if any
 from tax authorities. &amp;nbsp;When facts and circumstances change
 the Company reassesses these probabilities and records any changes in the consolidated financial statements as appropriate.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;In accordance with GAAP
 the Company is required to determine whether a tax position of the Company is more likely than not to be sustained upon examination by the applicable taxing authority
 including resolution of any related appeals or litigation processes
 based on the technical merits of the position. &amp;nbsp;The tax benefit to be recognized is measured as the largest amount of benefit that is greater than fifty percent likely of being realized upon ultimate settlement. &amp;nbsp;De-recognition of a tax benefit previously recognized could result in the Company recording a tax liability that would reduce stockholders&amp;#146; equity.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&apos;margin:0in 0in 0pt&apos;&gt;This policy also provides guidance on thresholds
 measurement
 de-recognition
 classification
 interest and penalties
 accounting in interim periods
 disclosure
 and transition that is intended to provide better financial statement comparability among different entities. &amp;nbsp;Management&amp;#146;s conclusions regarding this policy may be subject to review and adjustment at a later date based on factors including
 but not limited to

	height: 150px;
	overflow: auto;

	font-size: 1em;
}

The Company is a development stage enterprise and has accumulated operating losses since inception (May 2008) of $741
649
 and has had negative cash flows from operating activities during the period from inception (May 2008) through December 31
In March
 2014
 the Company raised $606
500 from the sale of 2
426
000 shares of common stock at a per share price of $.25. &nbsp;See Note 9
The accompanying financial statements have been prepared assuming that the Company will continue as a going concern
 which contemplates the recoverability of assets and the satisfaction of liabilities in the normal course of business.&nbsp;&nbsp;Since the Company recently raised capital through the sale of equity
In the event the Company does not generate sufficient funds from revenues or financing through the issuance of its common stock or from debt financing
 the Company may be unable to fully implement its business plan and pay its obligations as they become due
 any of which circumstances would have a material adverse effect on its business prospects
 financial condition
 and results of operations. The accompanying financial statements do not include any adjustments that might be required should the Company be unable to recover the value of its assets or satisfy its liabilities.

Disclose whether operations for the current or prior years generated sufficient cash to cover current obligations
 whether waivers were obtained from creditors relating to the company's default under the provisions of debt agreements and possible effects of such conditions and events
 such as: whether there is a possible need to obtain additional financing (debt or equity) or to liquidate certain holdings to offset future cash flow deficiencies. Disclose appropriate parent company information when parent is dependent upon remittances from subsidiaries to satisfy its obligations.

The preparation of financial statements in conformity with GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect certain reported amounts of assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements
The Company considers short-term interest bearing investments with initial maturities of three months or less to be cash equivalents. Cash and cash equivalents consist of cash in banks
The Company&#146;s taxable income or loss is included in the consolidated income tax returns of the Company&#146;s parent. Current and deferred income taxes are allocated to the members of the consolidated group as if each member were a separate taxpayer. The Company accounts for income taxes in accordance with FASB ASC Topic 740 &#147;Income Taxes
&#148; which requires accounting for deferred income taxes under the asset and liability method. &nbsp;Deferred income tax assets and liabilities are computed for the difference between the financial statement and tax bases of assets and liabilities that will result in taxable or deductible amounts in the future based on the enacted tax laws and rates applicable to the periods in which the differences are expected to affect taxable income. &nbsp;Valuation allowances are established
 when necessary
The determination of the Company&#146;s provision for income taxes requires significant judgment
 the use of estimates
 and the interpretation and application of complex tax laws. &nbsp;Significant judgment is required in assessing the timing and amounts of deductible and taxable items and the probability of sustaining uncertain tax positions. &nbsp;The benefits of uncertain tax positions are recorded in the Company&#146;s financial statements only after determining a more-likely-than-not probability that the uncertain tax positions will withstand challenge
 if any
 from tax authorities. &nbsp;When facts and circumstances change
In accordance with GAAP
 the Company is required to determine whether a tax position of the Company is more likely than not to be sustained upon examination by the applicable taxing authority
 including resolution of any related appeals or litigation processes
This policy also provides guidance on thresholds
 measurement
 de-recognition
 classification
 interest and penalties
 accounting in interim periods
 disclosure
 and transition that is intended to provide better financial statement comparability among different entities. &nbsp;Management&#146;s conclusions regarding this policy may be subject to review and adjustment at a later date based on factors including
 but not limited to
 on-going analyses of and changes to tax laws
 regulations and interpretations thereof. &nbsp;Generally
 the tax filings are no longer subject to income tax examinations by major taxing authorities for years before 2009. Any potential examinations may include questioning the timing and amount of deductions
 the nexus of income among various tax jurisdictions and compliance with U.S. federal
The Company recognizes interest accrued related to unrecognized tax benefits in interest expense and penalties in other operational expenses. No interest expense or penalties have been recognized as of and for the years ended December 31
The fair values of the Company&#146;s assets and liabilities that qualify as financial instruments under FASB ASC Topic 825
 &#147;Financial Instruments
&#148; approximate their carrying amounts presented in the accompanying financial statements at December 31
The Company complies with the accounting and disclosure requirements of FASB ASC 260
The calculation of diluted net loss per share excludes 1
225
000 warrants as of December 31
 2013 and 2012
The Company recognizes contingent losses that are both probable and estimable. &nbsp;In this context
 the Company defines probability as circumstances under which events are likely to occur. &nbsp;In regards to legal cost
 we record such costs as incurred.

var Show = {};
Show.LastAR = null
Show.hideAR = function(){
	Show.LastAR.style.display = 'none';
};
Show.showAR = function ( link
 id
 win ){
	if( Show.LastAR ){
		Show.hideAR();
	}
	var ref = link;
	do {
		ref = ref.nextSibling;
	} while (ref && ref.nodeName != 'TABLE');
	if (!ref || ref.nodeName != 'TABLE') {
		var tmp = win ?
			win.document.getElementById(id) :
			document.getElementById(id);
		if( tmp ){
			ref = tmp.cloneNode(true);
			ref.id = '';
			link.parentNode.appendChild(ref);
		}
	}
	if( ref ){
		ref.style.display = 'block';
		Show.LastAR = ref;
	}
};
Show.toggleNext = function( link ){
	var ref = link;
	do{
		ref = ref.nextSibling;
	}while( ref.nodeName != 'DIV' );
	if( ref.style &&
		ref.style.display &&
		ref.style.display == 'none' ){
		ref.style.display = 'block';
		if( link.textContent ){
			link.textContent = link.textContent.replace( '+'
 '-' );
		}else{
			link.innerText = link.innerText.replace( '+'
 '-' );
		}
	}else{
		ref.style.display = 'none';
		if( link.textContent ){
			link.textContent = link.textContent.replace( '-'
 '+' );
		}else{
			link.innerText = link.innerText.replace( '-'
 '+' );
		}
	}
};

The preparation of financial statements in conformity with GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect certain reported amounts of assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements
 as well as their related disclosures. &nbsp;Such estimates and assumptions also affect the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting period. &nbsp;Actual results could differ from those estimates.


Cash and Cash Equivalents
 Policy
The Company considers short-term interest bearing investments with initial maturities of three months or less to be cash equivalents. Cash and cash equivalents consist of cash in banks
 free credit on investment accounts and money market accounts. &nbsp;The Company has no cash or cash equivalents.


Income Taxes
 Policy
The Company&#146;s taxable income or loss is included in the consolidated income tax returns of the Company&#146;s parent. Current and deferred income taxes are allocated to the members of the consolidated group as if each member were a separate taxpayer. The Company accounts for income taxes in accordance with FASB ASC Topic 740 &#147;Income Taxes
&#148; which requires accounting for deferred income taxes under the asset and liability method. &nbsp;Deferred income tax assets and liabilities are computed for the difference between the financial statement and tax bases of assets and liabilities that will result in taxable or deductible amounts in the future based on the enacted tax laws and rates applicable to the periods in which the differences are expected to affect taxable income. &nbsp;Valuation allowances are established
 when necessary
The determination of the Company&#146;s provision for income taxes requires significant judgment
 the use of estimates
 and the interpretation and application of complex tax laws. &nbsp;Significant judgment is required in assessing the timing and amounts of deductible and taxable items and the probability of sustaining uncertain tax positions. &nbsp;The benefits of uncertain tax positions are recorded in the Company&#146;s financial statements only after determining a more-likely-than-not probability that the uncertain tax positions will withstand challenge
 if any
 from tax authorities. &nbsp;When facts and circumstances change
In accordance with GAAP
 the Company is required to determine whether a tax position of the Company is more likely than not to be sustained upon examination by the applicable taxing authority
 including resolution of any related appeals or litigation processes
This policy also provides guidance on thresholds
 measurement
 de-recognition
 classification
 interest and penalties
 accounting in interim periods
 disclosure
 and transition that is intended to provide better financial statement comparability among different entities. &nbsp;Management&#146;s conclusions regarding this policy may be subject to review and adjustment at a later date based on factors including
 but not limited to
 on-going analyses of and changes to tax laws
 regulations and interpretations thereof. &nbsp;Generally
 the tax filings are no longer subject to income tax examinations by major taxing authorities for years before 2009. Any potential examinations may include questioning the timing and amount of deductions
 the nexus of income among various tax jurisdictions and compliance with U.S. federal
 state and local tax laws.&nbsp; The Company's management does not expect that the total amount of unrecognized tax benefits will materially change over the next twelve months. 


        
The Company recognizes interest accrued related to unrecognized tax benefits in interest expense and penalties in other operational expenses. No interest expense or penalties have been recognized as of and for the years ended December 31
 2013 and 2012.


        
The fair values of the Company&#146;s assets and liabilities that qualify as financial instruments under FASB ASC Topic 825
 &#147;Financial Instruments
&#148; approximate their carrying amounts presented in the accompanying financial statements at December 31
 2013 and 2012.


        
The Company complies with the accounting and disclosure requirements of FASB ASC 260
The calculation of diluted net loss per share excludes 1
225
000 warrants as of December 31
 2013 and 2012
 since their effect is anti-dilutive. 


        
The Company recognizes contingent losses that are both probable and estimable. &nbsp;In this context
 the Company defines probability as circumstances under which events are likely to occur. &nbsp;In regards to legal cost
 we record such costs as incurred.

Effective May 31
 2011
 the Company and certain of its shareholders (Thomas Howells
 Travis Jenson
 Jenson Services
 Inc. and Kelly Trimble
 collectively
 the &#147;Principal Shareholders&#148;) entered into a Stock Purchase Agreement dated as of May 27
 2011 (&#147;SPA&#148;) with Safe Communications
 Inc.
 a Texas corporation n/k/a Kuboo
 Inc. (&#147;Buyer&#148;) under which the Buyer purchased for a $250
000 cash payment 10
000
000 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock
 representing 80% of the issued and outstanding common stock after giving effect to the purchase transaction. &nbsp;In addition
 under the SPA
 if the Buyer did not complete certain transactions within the time period prescribed by the SPA
 the Buyer would be obligated to pay the Company an additional $50
Effective May 31
 2011
 the Company also entered into a Principal Shareholders Agreement with each of the Principal Shareholders dated as of May 27
 2011 (&#147;PSA&#148;)
 under which the Company agreed to make payments to the Principal shareholders in the aggregate amount of $250
000
 in consideration of the Principal Shareholders&#146; undertakings in the SPA
 including but not limited to their agreement to indemnify the Buyer in connection with the stock purchase contemplated in the SPA. &nbsp;If the Buyer makes the additional $50
000 payment referenced above
 then the Company is required to pay such additional $50
000 to the Principal Shareholders in accordance with the PSA. The Company has not received any additional payment from the Buyer. Although the Company believes that it is not required to make the additional $50
000 payment to the Principal Shareholders until it receives such payment from the Buyer
 the Company has recorded a corresponding liability in the amount of $50
000. &nbsp;Each of the Principal Shareholders was a significant shareholder of the Company
 and
 in addition
 at the time of execution of the PSA
 Messrs. Howells
 Bassham and Jenson were directors of the Company
In connection with the closing of the transactions contemplated by the SPA
 effective May 31
 2011
 Travis Jenson resigned as President and Director of the Company
Wayne Bassham resigned as Treasurer and secretary of the Company. Mr. Bassham also tendered his resignation as a director of the Company
 effective ten days after the Company&#146;s mailing to its shareholders of an Information Statement on Schedule 14F-1. &nbsp;John P. Venners
 President of the Buyer
 was appointed interim President and a director of the Company
 effective May 31
 2011. &nbsp;Mr. Venners was appointed an officer and director of the Company by Wayne Bassham
 following the resignations of Messrs. Howells and Jenson
In connection with the closing of the stock purchase under the SPA
 the Buyer obtained control of the Company by acquiring 80% of the Company&#146;s issued and outstanding common stock and by having its designee
 John P. Venners
 President of the Buyer
Since May 31
 2011
 the date a change in control occurred
 the Company has occupied office space at the corporate office of its parent company
 Safe Communications
 Inc. (n/k/a Kuboo
 Inc.) (sometimes hereinafter referred to as &#147;Kuboo&#148;)
 which is provided at no cost. &nbsp;Kuboo incurs no incremental costs in providing this office space to the Company. &nbsp;At December 31
 2013
During the year ended December 31
 2013 and 2012
 Kuboo paid $36
936 and $35
248 respectively on behalf of the Company in payment of the Company&#146;s operating expenses
 consisting primarily of professional and other fees related to being a public company. These payments were treated as a contribution to the capital of the Company.
